  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1c45e10f-3142-4e5d-ab2d-cf34e62dd558'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer12841194254235815033">Hunters are a special breed, dedicated to tracking down treasures, magical beasts, and even other people. But such pursuits require a license, and less than one in a hundred thousand can pass the grueling qualification exam.   <span id="freeText12841194254235815033" style="display:none">Hunters are a special breed, dedicated to tracking down treasures, magical beasts, and even other people. But such pursuits require a license, and less than one in a hundred thousand can pass the grueling qualification exam. Those who do pass gain access to restricted areas, amazing stores of information, and the right to call themselves <i>Hunters</i>.<br /><br /><b>THE DAY OF DEPARTURE</b><br />Gon might be a country boy, but he has high aspirations. Despite his Aunt Mito's protests, Gon decides to follow in his father's footsteps and become a legendary Hunter. The Hunter hopefuls begin their journey by storm-tossed ship, where Gon meets Leorio and Kurapika, the only other applicants who aren't devastated by bouts of seasickness.<br /><br />Having survived the terrors of the high seas, Gon and his companions now have to prove their worth in a variety of tests in order to find the elusive Exam Hall. And once they get there, will they ever leave alive...?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1495095611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15818124953839374171"><b>Number of volumes: </b>33<br/><b>Number of chapters: </b>360<br/><b>Status:</b> on-going/currently on <s>damn</s> hiatus.<br/><b>Rating of the whole manga: </b>all the stars in the world. ∞<br/><br/>The anime is actually my favorite. After watching it about 3 times (twice 1999 and once 2011, however, I watched some episodes of the latter multiple times), I decided to read the manga. Hunter x Hunter is my favorite thing in the world. <br/>Hunter x Hunter tells the adventures of four young friends: Gon, Killua, Kurapika and Leorio. <p>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451943759i/17624473._SX540_.jpg' width='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <b>Minor spoilers</b></p></span>
  <span id="freeText15818124953839374171" style="display:none"><b>Number of volumes: </b>33<br><b>Number of chapters: </b>360<br><b>Status:</b> on-going/currently on <s>damn</s> hiatus.<br><b>Rating of the whole manga: </b>all the stars in the world. ∞<br><br>The anime is actually my favorite. After watching it about 3 times (twice 1999 and once 2011, however, I watched some episodes of the latter multiple times), I decided to read the manga. Hunter x Hunter is my favorite thing in the world. <br>Hunter x Hunter tells the adventures of four young friends: Gon, Killua, Kurapika and Leorio. <p>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451943759i/17624473._SX540_.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <b>Minor spoilers of the first few volumes, nothing major.</b>
  <br>
  <br>
</p><p>Hunters are the elite warriors. They have many privileges and can do some great achievements like discovering new species, capturing the most notorious criminals and discovering ruins.<br><br>It all starts when Gon Freecss decides to take the Hunter exam following his father's footsteps. After discovering that his father is the best hunter in the world and despite his aunt Mito-san's complaints, he's going to pass the exam and then do everything to find his father, Ging. In his journey, he befriends Kurapika, the last survivor of the Kurta Clan. He wants to avenge his people by becoming a blacklist Hunter, hunters who track down the most dangerous and wanted criminals. His people were massacred by the Phantom Troupe after stealing their scarlet eyes. One of the seven most beautiful things in the world. He also meets Leorio who wants to become a Doctor but unfortunately, needs money, so the Hunter exam seemed like a great opportunity to help him achieving his goal. And finally, Killua aka my favorite character and my anime crush, a former pro assassin. Not just any ex-assassin, his family is the most known in this field and unluckily for him, he's the favorite promising child.<br>He also encounters Hisoka, a creepy hot weird magician, and a very strong guy. Everyone seems to avoid him. And well, who can blame them?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493573598i/22630562._SY540_.jpg" alt="phantom troupe" width="300" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After watching the whole series, the exam looks so easy, honestly. Gon always finds people put in his way to help him to be stronger. No one can guess how our main characters will transform. We'll meet some outstanding fighters like Biscuit, Kite, Zeno and Silva, the greatest hunter Netero (the chairman) and some wicked villains like the beautiful Pitou, Feitan (I really like him even if he's evil) and Chrollo. Plus some other great characters who will steal your heart like Meruem and Alluka.<br><br><strong>I'll talk a little more about the characters before moving to the plot:</strong><br><br>When you have a huge set of characters (I already mentioned tons of names), you worry they'll be ignored, background decor, forgotten. What amazes me is how I still remember every person even though it's been a year since I last read/watched Hunter x Hunter. They're unforgettable. If you're a villain kind of person or any kind of person, you won't help but fall in love with the villains Togashi created. I love the phantom troupe even though they ruined my dear Kurapika's life. Their relationship, its complexity, their personalities will blow your mind. The chimera Ants villains (and I beg to differ) comes close, but we spend more time with the PT so we get to know them more. I can't help but mention Bomber, he annoyed to end. I despised him (not in a good way, like the way you're supposed to hate villains) because he annoyed me as a character to no end. I think Togashi could've done better but hey, that's only one in the midst of hundreds (or less).<br><strong> - Gon:</strong> he's ready to do anything for his friends. He might be hasty but he's so kind and courteous. People can't help but like him. He has a gentle heart. I'm telling you his father is extremely intelligent and will probably do anything to avoid meeting his kid and his friends especially. It might be very awkward, you know. Gon undergoes an amazing transformation, like most shonen main characters, he isn't the brightest but that doesn't stop him from stealing your heart. His adventure reshapes him. The friendships he makes, the experience they pass, will influence his personality a lot.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493573598i/22630560.jpg" alt="gonmeme" width="500" height="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><strong> - Killua:</strong> he's a Zoldyck, his family members are the most famous assassins of the Underworld. And he is so cute. His most famous word is Baka XD. Anyway, he's a rebel who hates their lifestyle. So he's craving his own way defying mostly his older brother Illumi. When he left he hit his mother. She cried. Tears of joy, her boy is a grown up now! That's how perfect his family is. So basically Hunter x Hunter is not only my favorite thing in the world but also features my most loved character ever. He's sharp, smart, vicious, assassin (was at a time but who cares?), will do anything to his friends (all of the squad will for that matter), kind (kinda), strong... I can talk about how perfect my little boy is all day.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493573598i/22630564._SX540_.jpg" alt="killua meme" width="500" height="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><strong> - Kurapika:</strong> he's (yes HE, unlike the popular first impression the blondie isn't a girl) an intelligent fellow. He will do the impossible to achieve his goals, but he won't let his disdain misguide him. Think and then act. <em>"Sometimes silence is the best answer."</em>  When I watched Yu Yu Hakusho, I noticed the uncanny similarities between Togashi's characters, Kurapika and Kurama. There's so similar, one might dislike it but I loved it! I like his resolve. How he never (well almost never) lets his anger to control him but uses his mind even in the most pressing situations. It's his best trait in my opinion.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493573598i/22630561._SX540_.jpg" alt="kurapikameme" width="500" height="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong> -Leorio:</strong> he might be a bit naive (he has his moments) but he's a good guy. Yeah, sometimes he might be stupid but in every squad, someone has to be like this I guess. His past helped him to become a better person, one who wants to help the weak. I like him the least. However, I can only say he really gets better later!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493573598i/22630563._SX540_.png" alt="leoriomeme" width="500" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong> - Hisoka:</strong> Gon is his pray and if you interfere he'll kill you. He's my number 2 favorite character in this series. He gets turned on by strong people yet I can't help but see him as a good guy, after all, because of him, Gon will be stronger. I'm not sure if he's a magician and/or a clown. But he <em>is</em> very strong. And yeah, his creepiness is hilarious. He's like an anti-hero. I'm not sure if he's straight because even though I ship him with Machi, a phantom troupe member, he surely has bisexual vibes. He's just a sociopath.<em> And I adore him for that. </em> I know he’s “problematic” and all but it’s Hisoka, you know?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493573598i/22630565._SX540_.jpg" alt="leoriomeme" width="500" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>What makes a good anime?<em> (at least for me)</em></strong><br></p> <br>	 continuous action?  ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 addicting and enjoyable story? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 character development? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 feels, lots of feels? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 no fan service? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 no power ups, no friendship bullshit? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 Strategy plans? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 memorable characters? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 a bit of romance? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔  <br>	 funny? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 HOT characters? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 Strong females? ✔ ✔ ✔  <br>	 unique and well developed story? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 thought provoking? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br>	 great animation? ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ ✔ <br> <br>Wow, that's a pretty accurate list, I think I'll use it in my future anime reviews (rating over 5).<br><br>Needless to say, I'll need to explain some points.<br><br>In many anime, we see the character just strong (especially shonen), rarely trains, and miraculously wins. This is not the case. We see Gon grow as a character, physically and mentally. In fact, he loses more than he wins even in important situations. I really liked that. I'm someone who loves action, fighting, blood, and I got all of that. The story has 8 arcs (counting the one in the manga), each handles different problems (will discuss them later) which allowed the story to cover different topics. It definitely questions your ethics, you won't know on which political side you stand, you'll shed tears for the villains (and sometimes want them to win). You'll watch episode after episode until you have finished all the 148 (146 not counting the recaps) and only want more.<br><br>It may seem childish and for kids at first. My friend told me it was hard to get into at first (of course, not for me lol) and I can see why. At first, the characters are introduced. The atmosphere is being built and you might expect sunshine and flowers. You can't be further from the truth. It gets savage and complicated. Especially with the <strong>Nen</strong> system. The most developed magic system I came across. Now looking back, I'm pretty sure I didn't understand what aura was or how exactly each person is classified. It took me a while to digest it when I was way older. <br><br>Honestly, many might throw their prejudgements and avoid watching this gem. It's childish, immature, stupid, they're 12 year olds! Look at their smiles! It's so long... Haha. These people don't know what they're missing. It only keeps getting better. The Yorknew and Chimera ant offers two of the best stories in shonen ever. They handle revenge, war, secret schemes, sacrifices, brotherhood even among the most wicked. Nothing is black and white. Nothing is predictable, the main character will kick everyone's ass? Not Gon. Not even Killua. Power comes in an illogical way? Not here. They undergo a hell of a training. <br>Do you like tournaments? Do you like aliens (or inhuman things yet are like people)? Do you want to see a game? Do you want politics? You to see treacherous brothers, psycho relatives, and numerous ways of torture? A devasting love story? A plot you can't in a million years predict? Strategies that will bore you to death but you will be rewarded by the best fights ever? You name it and I guarantee that you will find it here.<br><p><br>Yoshihiro Togashi suffers from back pain. Hunter x Hunter started in 1998, Naruto in 1999. While HxH has only 360 released chapters, Naruto 700. Might I also add that Naruto copied Hunter x Hunter?! Anyway, you can only guess the pain of waiting. Some chapters were released last year (been on hiatus since 2014) and now we're still waiting for chapter 361. It's killing us the fans.<br><br>The art isn't the best. If we had to give up Togashi's drawing style and have the rest of the story, I wouldn't mind. I mean, of course, no one will catch the characters' impressions like he does (especially, Hisoka), I'm ready to sacrifice it to know what will happen.<br><br>Many complain from his writing style, I have to admit, it gets so bad at some point. He obviously suffers from back pain but he wants to do his best. I respect him for that. I'm thinking about rereading it, though. I missed it so much. I want to buy it some day. And saying I want to reread it is something because I never reread books.<br></p><p><br><b><u><i>PS: Some names in my review differ a little from the manga. I used the names of the anime. </i></u></b> <br><i>I'm really grateful for a dear friend. If she reads this, she'll know herself. Thanks, S for reminding me of how great this show is.</i></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="15818124953839374171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Off he goes to the trials – but will he blah blah of course he will eventually and find his dad and zzzzzzzzzzzz… <br /><br />Hunter X Hunter Volume 1 sets up the series premise and the first obstacles Gon and his fellow wannabes have to overcome - and I couldn’t have cared less!   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2390402610?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Artemy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Artemy" href="/user/show/39811979-artemy">Artemy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20496208-hunter-x-hunter-vol-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39811979-artemy?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2390402610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9577050961724089579">Hunter x Hunter is yet another popular shonen manga, generally similar to stuff like Dragon Ball, Fullmetal Alchemist, Naruto, My Hero Academia, etc. This one is about a fictional fantasy world where hunter is one of the most prestigious and well-paid jobs, so everybody wants to be one but very few people are actually qualified, since you have to go through a series of very tough and rigorous tests to get certified. It’s also worth mentioning that in this world, being a hunter is more akin to be</span>
  <span id="freeText9577050961724089579" style="display:none">Hunter x Hunter is yet another popular shonen manga, generally similar to stuff like Dragon Ball, Fullmetal Alchemist, Naruto, My Hero Academia, etc. This one is about a fictional fantasy world where hunter is one of the most prestigious and well-paid jobs, so everybody wants to be one but very few people are actually qualified, since you have to go through a series of very tough and rigorous tests to get certified. It’s also worth mentioning that in this world, being a hunter is more akin to being a hero and keeping the peace — they don’t usually kill animals for sport. Gon is the young Son Goku-looking protagonist of the book, and he has some extraordinary instincts that make it clear that he’s going to become a hunter in the future. The book has a fairly standard shonen setup, and judging by the first volume not much about it stands out so far. But I am always a sucker for a long series with a lighthearted tone that can take me on a journey filled with adventures, so I really enjoyed my time with this volume anyway. Based on all the praise I hear about this series, I have no doubt that it only gets better as the story progresses, so I am looking forward to more volumes of HxH in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9577050961724089579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6235300924929332193"><i>
  <b>4 of 5 stars<br/><br/>-----</b>
</i><br/><br/><i>"Being fooled is as good as being dead" </i><br/><br/>Oh, how I missed these guysss! <br/><br/>I finished watching the anime adaptation of Hunter x Hunter less than a month ago and I am still unable to moved on. I can't shake the emptiness I felt after watching it and all I wanted was more of this HxH world so I decided to start reading the manga. Though I don't know if it was a good idea since it was still on going and on hiatus. <br/><br/>The hunter applicants, including our main character Gon, Killua, Kur</span>
  <span id="freeText6235300924929332193" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>4 of 5 stars<br /><br />-----</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>"Being fooled is as good as being dead" </i><br /><br />Oh, how I missed these guysss! <br /><br />I finished watching the anime adaptation of Hunter x Hunter less than a month ago and I am still unable to moved on. I can't shake the emptiness I felt after watching it and all I wanted was more of this HxH world so I decided to start reading the manga. Though I don't know if it was a good idea since it was still on going and on hiatus. <br /><br />The hunter applicants, including our main character Gon, Killua, Kurapika and Leorio, is now in the middle of the first phase of the exam. Everyone is in the state of both panic and confusion, except Hisoka who's now showing his bloodlust. Well, it was given that he was triggered to kill by the other applicants who tried to get in his way, atleast in the anime. It was a good excuse for him to kill anyway. But here in manga, it was shown that he acted as a judge even though no one triggered him to fight. I don't know how close the characters' development in the anime compared to the manga, but I'm excited to see for myself.</span>

  <span id="freeText17515702039602598770" style="display:none">I’ve been pretty wary of starting this series because it’s on an indefinite hiatus. But I saw it being lonely on the library bookshelf and was like “Aw. Well... it’s worth a shot.”<br /><br />I’m so glad I tried this!! The story is FABULOUS. It’s better than the author’s previous series “YuYu Hakusho” in some aspects. It’s a stereotypical fighting manga with a ton of cliches but it’s cute and epic?? So whatevs it’s cool with me. <br /><br />The pacing is well done, characters are compelling and at the very least interesting, and the art is endearing. Everything is a certain style. It’s not poorly done, but it’s not for everyone. <br /><br />(Also? That thank you note from him to the author of Sailor Moon was adorable. It basically said she helped him out coloring pages and he likes her art work. [spoiler alert they get married!])</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14974770026955150285">Chapter 1 is actually a shock to me. I never expected manga will be like this. I have watched all 148 episodes of hunter x hunter for 3 times and I never imagine that the actual happenings are like this. I find it really cute. I just love it!<br/><br/>Chapter 2 is the incident from the huge storm. Gon shows his great sense of observation. The manga shows more details about this than in the anime which is cool. Also, there’s just a lot of difference to the manga and anime. <br/><br/>Chapter 3 is when Gon, Kurapika, </span>
  <span id="freeText14974770026955150285" style="display:none">Chapter 1 is actually a shock to me. I never expected manga will be like this. I have watched all 148 episodes of hunter x hunter for 3 times and I never imagine that the actual happenings are like this. I find it really cute. I just love it!<br /><br />Chapter 2 is the incident from the huge storm. Gon shows his great sense of observation. The manga shows more details about this than in the anime which is cool. Also, there’s just a lot of difference to the manga and anime. <br /><br />Chapter 3 is when Gon, Kurapika, and Leorio arrive at Dolle’s port and they are looking for the right way to the examination place. Leorio’s actions are still the same. I like that he is realistically high tempered and impatient but still has a good heart. I just love their differences. They are all unique and a perfect fit as friends.<br /><br />Chapter 4 is when they walk through that dark path to find the navigators. Gon is still that great little child with an applauding sense of observation. I also really like Gon because he is just cute (not only as a child but his character, too) and though in this manga Kurapika is highlighted as the “smart one”, Gon is also smart when it comes to critical thinking on practical sense. Gon also manifest great bravery.<br /><br />Chapter 5 is when they are sent by the navigators to the hunter examination place. Oh, the funny thing in this Chapter is that they really have food in the elevator! LOL. Tompa is still the same. An asshole. This chapter is almost the same as the anime.<br /><br />Chapter 6 is when the first stage of their examination starts. Also, this is the time where they meet Killua. The two are just so cute but for Killua to be hot at an early age is just unfair lol.<br /><br />Chapter 7 is when they are in the middle of their marathon. Everyone is quitting because of the strain and stress of not knowing when the end of the tunnel is. This chapter is pretty much the same with the anime. There are just differences with Gon’s story when he mentioned it to Killua and also the time when Gon and Killua did a challenge at the end of the tunnel. <br /><br />Chapter 8 is when they are already on their way to the second phase. The happenings are different somehow. Killua talks a lot here, Leorio and Kurapika are in a pinch and Leorio got wounded. Kurapika is still as sharp as ever.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14974770026955150285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1606764176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1606764176" />
    <a title="Jordan Stephens" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13357710-jordan-stephens"><img alt="Jordan Stephens" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544176100p2/13357710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1606764176?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jordan Stephens" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jordan Stephens" href="/user/show/13357710-jordan-stephens">Jordan Stephens</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13357710-jordan-stephens?shelf=books-i-read-growing-up">books-i-read-growing-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13357710-jordan-stephens?shelf=favorite-manga">favorite-manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13357710-jordan-stephens?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13357710-jordan-stephens?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1606764176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3317781926521548239">This manga does everything a shounen manga should do. When I think of the perfect manga, I think of Hunter X Hunter. This review is about the series as a whole.<br/><br/>The fights are amazing. Each hunter has their own ability and fighting style. The main characters use their wits and their own unique style to win. I liked Dragon Ball Z as much as the next kid growing up, but each characters strength is determined by their power level, and that's about it (DragonBall is a different). In HxH there is so m</span>
  <span id="freeText3317781926521548239" style="display:none">This manga does everything a shounen manga should do. When I think of the perfect manga, I think of Hunter X Hunter. This review is about the series as a whole.<br /><br />The fights are amazing. Each hunter has their own ability and fighting style. The main characters use their wits and their own unique style to win. I liked Dragon Ball Z as much as the next kid growing up, but each characters strength is determined by their power level, and that's about it (DragonBall is a different). In HxH there is so much thought and strategy during the fights. When a character wins, you feel like they deserved it.<br /><br />The characters are memorable and fun. If pressed I could name 10's of characters from this series. They are as unique as their abilities. Some shounen rely on the same types of characters you see over and over again (especially the villains). In HxH the villains are some of the best part, they are well thought out and entertaining to watch.<br /><br />The story isn't groundbreaking, but done it's brilliantly. The overarching story is that Gon wants to find his father. However, like most ongoing manga, there are various story arcs. We see Gon mature and encounter various trials as he develops as a hunter and helps his friends.<br /><br />The art is on and off. Having started the series over a decade ago, back in 2004ish, I've experienced the many writing hiatuses of Togashi. There are times when the art is wonderful, and fits the story beautifully. Other times, there are issues when it's clear the art isn't quite as strong. Personally, this was never a huge issue for me (the art, not the breaks). Any new chapter was better than no new chapter.<br /><br />Simply put, HxH is my jam. I've read the manga multiple times and watched more than one version of the anime. I've probably spent more time with Gon and Killua than I have with any other manga/anime characters. It is both a manga and anime (the 2011 version) that I can wholeheartedly recommend with no reservations. <br /><br />Be aware that this series, while for all intents and purposes is currently finished, isn't truly ended. Gon still has room to grow, and there are plenty of adventures for him to have. His journey as a hunter has just begun; his adventures with his friends only just started. I've had to realize that I might not get to read all of his adventures, and maybe I was foolish to think I could. I've waited with bated breath many a year for more HxH through the many hiatuses. But ultimately I've come to understand that mangakas are people too. Unlike a novel, manga span hundreds and hundreds of chapters that have to be both written and drawn. It's taken time, but I can look back on my HxX experience as a whole and have unabashed and total love for the series. Thank you Togashi, and thank you HxH.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3317781926521548239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_340628785" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/340628785" />
    <a title="jecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4185654-jecca"><img alt="jecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599701510p2/4185654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/340628785?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jecca" href="/user/show/4185654-jecca">jecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer340628785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3224401969569948354">Rating:<br/>Art: 5/5 <br/>Story: 5/5<br/><br/>My rating scale for this--and all subsequent volumes--will be based on story and art. I caught an episode of the 2011 anime on Animax and I realized, hey, I never knew what happened after the Zoaldyck arc (back when it was on GMA). I was also in the mood to read something gory, so I decided to read the manga. <br/><br/>Gon Freecss, 11 going on 12, is off to take the prestigious Hunter exam above the objections of his adoptive mother, Mito. The exam is an arduous one, where it is </span>
  <span id="freeText3224401969569948354" style="display:none">Rating:<br />Art: 5/5 <br />Story: 5/5<br /><br />My rating scale for this--and all subsequent volumes--will be based on story and art. I caught an episode of the 2011 anime on Animax and I realized, hey, I never knew what happened after the Zoaldyck arc (back when it was on GMA). I was also in the mood to read something gory, so I decided to read the manga. <br /><br />Gon Freecss, 11 going on 12, is off to take the prestigious Hunter exam above the objections of his adoptive mother, Mito. The exam is an arduous one, where it is said that only one in hundreds of thousands can pass the test (personally, I think this is an exaggeration especially when one sees the amount of Hunters they meet in later volumes). Even if this is the cases, thousands still take the exam every year as being a Hunter gives you the best privileges in the world as well as access to places, things and occupations. <br /><br />The first volume tackles the process of the Hunter exam. As soon as Gon steps off Whale Island, the exam begins. Because of the volume of people who want to take the exam every year, the elimination process starts on the transport he takes to the exam center. Here, he meets fellow examinees Kurapika and Leorio. Only the three of them pass the standards and are brought to a meeting place where they'll meet a navigator to take them to the test site. This also turns out to be a test which they also pass. They finally reach the hidden exam site. They meet recurring Hunter Exam takers Tonpa, Amori brothers, etc. During the first round, an endurance test, Gon befriends Killua Zoldyck<br />the only other examinee his age. Backgrounds for the other characters are revealed during the run: Killua comes from an assassin family and is rebelling by taking the Hunter Exam, Kurapika wants to be a Hunter to hunt down a bandit group [Genei Ryodan] who killed his tribe for their scarlet eyes and get access to places (rich collectors, black market, etc) where he can find their eyes, and Leorio wants the riches being a Hunter can provide to become a doctor for the poor.<br /><br />During the test, examinee Hisoka (disqualified from last years examination since he killed a judge) decides to help with the selection process by getting rid of the weaker competition. The introduction of Hisoka is the first scene of gore and violence in the manga. <br /><br />The manga is interesting and exciting, especially since half of the lead characters are morally ambiguous and have darkness in them. The details in the art are great, from backgrounds to shading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3224401969569948354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1092156125396396472">	Hunters are specially trained workers who's fields range from gourmet hunters to assassins. All Hunters must take the deadly and excruciating Hunter Exam, planned out by determined task makers, to receive their Hunters license. Gon is a nature loving boy who wants to become a Hunter to gain access to all restricted areas to search for his missing father. The story is narrated to make Gon’s test the main story storyline. When Gon leaves to finally take the exam, he teams up with two other exam t</span>
  <span id="freeText1092156125396396472" style="display:none">	Hunters are specially trained workers who's fields range from gourmet hunters to assassins. All Hunters must take the deadly and excruciating Hunter Exam, planned out by determined task makers, to receive their Hunters license. Gon is a nature loving boy who wants to become a Hunter to gain access to all restricted areas to search for his missing father. The story is narrated to make Gon’s test the main story storyline. When Gon leaves to finally take the exam, he teams up with two other exam takers, Leorio a doctor, and Kurapika the lone survivor of the massacre on his home village. The exam proves to be difficult, taking place in settings like forests, swamps, a trick tower over a thousand feet tall, and in the middle of the ocean. <br />	I found this book amazingly fun to read and I often found myself laughing at the jokes hidden in the text. The only weakness of these books is that you would have to truly love manga to know how to read this book, since it is Japanese format. Which is my favorite type of manga. This book series is slightly violent but in a clever way that makes the reader try to find the possibilities of that character dying. I would definitely recommend this book to a classmate or two, but only the ones who I know wouldn’t make fun of manga later. I plan to revisit the library again to finish up over 30 other books to this series.<br />	To Ms.Gaston: The books I read were a books 1 through 3, so this review is for the 3 volumes together. I have counted the total pages and that is why the # is high. </span>

<div id="review_1083109852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083109852" />
    <a title="Dana Salman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2246621-dana-salman"><img alt="Dana Salman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454265334p2/2246621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083109852?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Salman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Salman" href="/user/show/2246621-dana-salman">Dana Salman</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20496208-hunter-x-hunter-vol-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083109852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10551681416101388303">So this is my first time reading <i>Hunter x Hunter</i>. I've decided I'll never read either <i>Naruto</i> or <i>Bleach</i>, and that's mostly because they're too long and I've already committed myself to a long-running manga (<i>One Piece</i>), and plus I was never interested. But I've heard great things about <i>Hunter x Hunter</i>. I remember seeing this show (the original anime) in Arabic dub on Spacetoon, and I watched the first few episodes but got bored a little too quickly. Now however there's a new anime that's truer to </span>
  <span id="freeText10551681416101388303" style="display:none">So this is my first time reading <i>Hunter x Hunter</i>. I've decided I'll never read either <i>Naruto</i> or <i>Bleach</i>, and that's mostly because they're too long and I've already committed myself to a long-running manga (<i>One Piece</i>), and plus I was never interested. But I've heard great things about <i>Hunter x Hunter</i>. I remember seeing this show (the original anime) in Arabic dub on Spacetoon, and I watched the first few episodes but got bored a little too quickly. Now however there's a new anime that's truer to the manga, and I can't wait to watch it. Gonna read the manga first though, cause that's a rule I have - manga always comes first (just like books come before the movie).<br /><br />So far it's pretty entertaining, but if I have one gripe (and this may sound silly) it's this: don't people die a little too often in this manga?? I mean it's not rare in genres like seinen and horror, but this is a shounen - hardly anyone ever dies in those! Also, Gon is only 12 years old - he's not a little bit fazed by how easily the other contestants get picked off? Oh well it's still the first volume; I suppose I'll get used to it...</span>
  <a data-text-id="10551681416101388303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer696313107" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18177170506417062271">Over-the-top. That's what makes it fun.<br/><br/>A friend recommended this to me, saying it was a "deconstruction." Now, I've encountered deconstructions in the past *looks at Madoka and sighs* so I was a little hesitant to pick this one up. My friend swore it was really, really good, and so I decided to give it a try.<br/><br/>For those unaware of what deconstructed means, it's basically "take the most basic tropes, cliches, and conventions of a genre and play them straight, regardless of what the results." (see <a href='http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/GenreDeconstruction' rel='nofollow noopener'>T</a></span>
  <span id="freeText18177170506417062271" style="display:none">Over-the-top. That's what makes it fun.<br /><br />A friend recommended this to me, saying it was a "deconstruction." Now, I've encountered deconstructions in the past *looks at Madoka and sighs* so I was a little hesitant to pick this one up. My friend swore it was really, really good, and so I decided to give it a try.<br /><br />For those unaware of what deconstructed means, it's basically "take the most basic tropes, cliches, and conventions of a genre and play them straight, regardless of what the results." (see <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/GenreDeconstruction" rel="nofollow noopener">TV Tropes</a> for more information)<br /><br />This series does exactly that, and the results vary a bit, but overall, if you think of it as a parody, it's actually quite good. I can't speak for how good it is if you don't realize the deconstruction/parody aspect, since I went in informed of this, but it was fun to me.<br /><br />If you like Shounen, and if you enjoyed Yu Yu Hakusho, you'll find this entertaining.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93902080-mert?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93902080-mert?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93902080-mert?shelf=manga">manga</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2744113926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11524020501464605123"><b>5/5 Stars (%94/100)</b><br/><br/>Another shonen manga that inspired me as much as Naruto. I've watched the anime first then proceeded to read the manga. It is brilliant because of the very interesting story and the well-written characters. Gon is a funny and dumb protagonist type whereas his best friend Killua is very serious and calm. There is Hisoka as a trickster (joker) figure. The idea of the hunter is brilliant, both the characters and the story is interesting. However, Togashi DID NOT finish the manga.</span>
  <span id="freeText11524020501464605123" style="display:none"><b>5/5 Stars (%94/100)</b><br /><br />Another shonen manga that inspired me as much as Naruto. I've watched the anime first then proceeded to read the manga. It is brilliant because of the very interesting story and the well-written characters. Gon is a funny and dumb protagonist type whereas his best friend Killua is very serious and calm. There is Hisoka as a trickster (joker) figure. The idea of the hunter is brilliant, both the characters and the story is interesting. However, Togashi DID NOT finish the manga. He previously left the manga so it was finished by others. He did the same with the manga so it is not complete. (Most of the big story arcs are finished though.) The last arc is not complete but the arc that anime ended with is also completed in the manga. Definitely suggested.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11524020501464605123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246423972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16904945908195950953">(just for the record, this is a slight alteration of my anime review) <br/><br/>Hunter x Hunter easily ranks amongst the most interesting shounen manga ever made. At the same time, it is also amongst the most frustrating ones, as it has several mishaps.<br/><br/>Let’s start with the story. It’s about a little boy named Gon, looking for his father who is a Hunter, a super mercenary of sorts travelling the world and doing missions and quests. Like finding something rare or arresting a wanted criminal. So in the conte</span>
  <span id="freeText16904945908195950953" style="display:none">(just for the record, this is a slight alteration of my anime review) <br /><br />Hunter x Hunter easily ranks amongst the most interesting shounen manga ever made. At the same time, it is also amongst the most frustrating ones, as it has several mishaps.<br /><br />Let’s start with the story. It’s about a little boy named Gon, looking for his father who is a Hunter, a super mercenary of sorts travelling the world and doing missions and quests. Like finding something rare or arresting a wanted criminal. So in the context of the story, that little boy decides that the best way to find him is to become one himself. And here you are, having a 12 year old boy rivalling hundreds of tough adult grunts for the rank of Hunter.<br /><br />Sounds stupid doesn’t it? Especially when taking into account that he is totally weak, unskilled and his personality is like that of a saint inside a den of cannibals. Well, frankly it is. It is frakking impossible to buy it. The story does a good job at showing how friendship and teamwork can work through all that but it still is damn hard to buy it. Anyways, this is just the core story … and it gets nowhere. The boy never finds his father. In fact, this hardly matters as much as everything else in terms of character development or side stories. Which are both a lot in numbers and of a good level of storytelling. <br /><br />Well, that is not really the point. The whole story is actually about a team of kids (and an almost token adult) passing tests and facing difficulties, as means to develop their skills and achieve their goals. Heck, 90% of the plot is either doing quests, duels or simple research in order to get to that meagre 10% of actual progress in the story. And to the most part is slow and dull. I am fully aware that this anime is famous for being the exact opposite of slow and dull. But what I am referring to here is the pacing. Very few things happen in each episode and even those are done in a non-exciting way. This is mostly a problem of the poor use of cinematics the sections of animation and sound have, rather than the actual story.<br /><br />The artwork is average to bad, with minimalistic character figures, simple lighting effects, and usually weak motion effects. It imporves along the way but it never looks great. For a long period of time the battles aren’t that many in numbers or not very exciting like in most shounen action manga. That is of course excused by the fact the characters in the beginning were weak and possessed no major special powers. That still makes it feel dull and drops the reread value. But it is wrong to see this as a fighting action series alone. Most confrontations, although very simple in choreography, have lots of wits and it is brains and not muscles that matter in most of them. That by the way does not save the artwork from feeling boring. With proper handling, even a turtle sleeping can look amazing. And with all these frozen panels, generic character figures, and semi-interesting major battles, this isn’t what I’m talking about. <br /><br />Now back to the pacing. As I said, the initial chapters can be excused to be uneventful because they focus on getting to know the characters, as well as to keep in touch with the simple fact they are wimps. Not really a negative but it does make a lot of them to have no reason to read twice. The magic of Media Res could help to start at a more exciting point in the plot and just present the rest as flashbacks or something. Anyways, the first dozen chapters are just to get to know them and then up to half of the series on how they pass the Hunter exam. It is still not much of a story and it’s the characters and their individual side stories that keep you interested. After that, the second half slowly makes the characters stronger and some missions get really serious, as professional killers enter and things get far more dangerous. At this point, the manga became a more traditional shounen type story and to be honest has more meat to keep watching. Plus it didn’t take out the feeling of strategy and wits in battles. Thus it really is the same, only better. It improves to the point where you feel you are watching Dragonball Z but with more wits… Still not much of a story though. And Gon’s father is nothing but a vague backdrop by now. Seriously, up until the third arc Gon is hardly doing anything; it’s just his friend getting his revenge. Then there is this vague mission of looking for him but the objective is very vague and still distant.<br /><br />I have a very negative impression of how the manga develops later on. What’s going on with the arc goals anyway? First they want to become Hunters and THEN they train to become strong? Doesn’t that make the whole title of a Hunter feel piss poor? Shouldn’t it be the other way around? And then what the hell was that business with the videogame? The third arc is about raising money to buy a game. Does that seem a logical upscale from someone taking part in deadly tournaments to be arm-wrestling for a videogame? Or an entire arc just playing that very videogame while gathering cards as if it’s a Yu-Gi-Oh rip-off? The fourth arc ain’t much better; now they are hunting bugs. Why are the arcs going in reverse in terms of build up? What will their ultimate challenge be; to save a cat from a tree? It felt like the story starts with the lead wanting to become big macho Hokage and slowly making him return back to Ninja Kindergarten. <br /><br />Not to mention the whole business of the videogame, this strikes me as nothing but crude marketing promotion of videogames and card games. They threw away the initial premise of a boy going on an adventure to find his lost father and replaced it with “buy card games and play videogames” commercials. I mean, come on, the story became “pay ten million bucks to play a videogame where you gather cards that will combine into the super card that will magically grand you a wish like the goddamn Dragonballs.” And did I just saw a cute girl transform into a brute male adult somewhere in there? What horsesh*t is this? Where did the pure feeling of the beginning go to? Furthermore the story is not over yet, but the mangaka is making a new chapter at a much slower pace than before, as if he reached a writer’s block. That is not very good.<br /><br />By the way, I’d be damned if Kishimoto didn’t rip off the Hunter Exam arc to make the Chuunin Exam arc in Naruto, as well as the red eyes of a vengeful friend. <br /><br />So the characters are the meat of the story and it’s quite the likable cast as far as shounen go. Each one of the major and secondary characters is given a rather high amount of attention and “usually” some development other than his superpowers. They are still far from fully fleshed out characters though. Gon for example is impossible to relate to as everything is in his eyes one big rainbow of joy. You can stab him in the heart only to hear him asking for forgiveness because his blood stained your knife. As much as good hearted as he may be, he has no chance of surviving in the jungle that is the human civilization like that. Heck, let’s face it, he managed to become a Hunter only because all the super fighters he faced refused to hurt him. Although not completely two-dimensional, they all lack real depth or even reasonable reactions. As for catharsis, well, Gon’s father is not found and the revenge thing was not completed, so nothing here either. Not to forget mentioning how everything feels like going in reverse from wanting to become Hokage to saving cats from trees (random parallelism). What you get are semi-developed characters at best, whose backdrop is quite the typical shounen archetype formula. <br /><br />Down to it, it still is a good shounen, as its internal logic surpasses most of everything in the genre. Most quests require strategy, field tactics, even psychology to overcome and it’s only much later where characters get all DBZ that “my battle power is greater than yours” becomes an issue. Even then, the reason “this power beats that power” is also excused nicely. But it still is not a series you watch for the battles as I said numerous times, they are few major ones and they are all handled poorly. I mean, the show is full of people being eaten alive by monsters or killed horribly by top assassins and yet it makes it feel like you are feeding ducks over at the park lake. Seriously, with different handling it could easily become a horror / survival to the most part. Yet all you get is Gon saying “Let’s be friends” while all around him people are nihilistically chewed alive by monsters or are decapitated by yawning assassins. This is a shounen series but, geez, the context is way off. If you are not willing to show it at its proper way, don’t show it at all. Atmosphere failure; that alone made the show half-likable. <br /><br />Bottom line. Although terribly similar to Naruto (and damn ripped off by it), it really is superior to it, despite the worse artwork and reverse build up. And since most people still consider Naruto to be amongst the top fighting shounen around (not me; I’m too smart to fall for that), that means it’s good stuff. Yet at the same time it lacks the tension of most modern shounens in terms of atmosphere and that can make its superior tactics and deep character immersion to lose a lot of credit. <br /><br />In other news, other shows like Kaiji or Liar Game eat its tactics for breakfast, and Full Metal Alchemist does an overall far better job in terms of action, character immersion, and proper use of cinematics. You have been informed.</span>

  <span id="freeText16224536474226627793" style="display:none">So I finally got around to giving this a shot, and I gotta say that so far I really like it! c:<br /><br />From the get-go, it reminds me quite a bit of Dragon Ball (with Gon being very similar to Goku in both temperament and appearance) with a bit of Naruto thrown in, which I really enjoyed. The hunting aspect is interesting, and while I'm still not entirely sure what being a "hunter" entails, despite the few explanations so far (seems to be a combined animal hunter, treasure hunter, protector, etc. mishmash), I'm interested to learn more. <br /><br />The different tests that they've had to pass to even GET to the hunter exam (...and boy I did NOT expect there to be an exam-like aspect to this book) were really interesting. The beginning bit with the ship basically taking out a huge number of potential hunters through sea sickness was hilarious, and then having Gon basically making friends with people he maybe shouldn't be making friends with was even better. <div id="review_3616834964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3616834964" />
    <a title="Daniel Ocón" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24483056-daniel-oc-n"><img alt="Daniel Ocón" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590601332p2/24483056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3616834964?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Ocón" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Ocón" href="/user/show/24483056-daniel-oc-n">Daniel Ocón</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3616834964&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3616834964" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4933468640920163582">The manga as a whole, at least up to the Chimera Arc, is certainly worth a read.<br/><br/>The beginning is not great. Certainly unique, subverting expectations -something that this story does a lot, both to its benefit and detriment-, but narratively is kind of a mess. First of all, for an adventure manga there's not a lot of thrill: the MC and his companions breeze through the entire Hunter Exam without much obstacle, they're in a whole other level compared to the rest of competitors and no element lasts</span>
  <span id="freeText4933468640920163582" style="display:none">The manga as a whole, at least up to the Chimera Arc, is certainly worth a read.<br /><br />The beginning is not great. Certainly unique, subverting expectations -something that this story does a lot, both to its benefit and detriment-, but narratively is kind of a mess. First of all, for an adventure manga there's not a lot of thrill: the MC and his companions breeze through the entire Hunter Exam without much obstacle, they're in a whole other level compared to the rest of competitors and no element lasts enough to be properly developed. Second, this exam is filled with non-Nen users but Nen users have such an enormous advantage that it's kind of pointless, just let Nen users be the only ones to become Hunters. Oh wait, the ARE the only ones who can become hunters!<br /><br />The "messy" argument applies when you take into consideration that the next arc, after Killua's rescue, is about how, even if you have a Hunter's Licence, it doesn't activate until you train your Nen skills. So not only were people killed because of nothing, but the entire Hunter Exam is a big useless event.<br /><br />Not that the first arcs are worthless. They're certainly entertaining, with the whole Hisoka and Gon ordeal being pretty satisfying, and the encounters have an incredible amount of creativity put in display -even if, on themselves, the strategies are not very thoughtful- but the combination of the elements shine light on a bigger inconsistency problem.<br /><br />The third arc is about our main characters, Gon and Killua, going into an arm-wrestling competition. However, they're not the center of attention, since another member of the group named Kurapika finds himself in a body-guarding job with the mafia, in which he encounters the Phantom Troupe, who murdered his entire clan.<br /><br />To those versed in anime, Kurapika is just the original Sasuke. This arc is splendid. And also when subversion becomes a problem. See, all the events have an amazing build-up, the tension is sky-high and the action, pretty brief (subversion from the standard 12-episode-fight), is absolutely brutal. But the resolution is weak, subversion for the sake of subversion.<br /><br />And Hunter x Hunter makes this so much worse: Gon loses his arm twice in the series and always gets it back. Yes, it's subversive to not have long lasting consequences, but that also means you have no real progression. Gon does horrible things at the end of the Chimera Arc, loses people, should be traumatized. But nope, he's dandy. Roll it up, boys.<br /><br />The show also has a major problem with fetishes. Even before all the furry shit in Chimera Arc, it treats a pedophile as a fun guy, implies that a child was raped by stranger women his entire childhood, has a bunch of goth chicks in the background and introduces a cross-dresser as a Deus Ex Machina whose wishes disolve all the tension (yeah folks, Alluka is just a fetish, because the entire Zoldryck family is a parade of weirdo deviants).<br /><br />If you watch the anime, you'll think that the art is pleasant. It is... sometimes. The first volumes specially are really messy, detail losing itself among the ink. The drawing has this feline quality that I personally really like, only prevalent in the 99' adaptation and lost for the remake.<br /><br />And this is Hunter x Hunter. Greatness buried along a mess that sometimes sticks, bringing together masterful pieces of storytelling: the Yorknew Arc or the LESSER, but still good Chimera Arc. Overall it's good, even the worst plot has nice and creative powers, interactions and so on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4933468640920163582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="updateActionLinks">

<div id="review_3514371340" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3514371340" />
    <a title="Maria Bazarte-De La Luz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48196112-maria-bazarte-de-la-luz"><img alt="Maria Bazarte-De La Luz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600451261p2/48196112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3514371340?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Bazarte-De La Luz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Bazarte-De La Luz" href="/user/show/48196112-maria-bazarte-de-la-luz">Maria Bazarte-De La Luz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3514371340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16734509755584515418">In the first volume of Hunter x Hunter, we meet Gon and other friends he meets along the way. Gon wants to become a hunter, which is one of the most respected and well-paying jobs. He wants to become a hunter because his father is/was one. However, it is very difficult to become a hunter. There are phases to an exam that not many people pass. Especially not newcomers. In this volume we also meet Leorio, Kirupica, Killua, and other examinees that could be dangerous. <br/><br/>I enjoyed this volume, but the</span>
  <span id="freeText16734509755584515418" style="display:none">In the first volume of Hunter x Hunter, we meet Gon and other friends he meets along the way. Gon wants to become a hunter, which is one of the most respected and well-paying jobs. He wants to become a hunter because his father is/was one. However, it is very difficult to become a hunter. There are phases to an exam that not many people pass. Especially not newcomers. In this volume we also meet Leorio, Kirupica, Killua, and other examinees that could be dangerous. <br /><br />I enjoyed this volume, but the characters still seem a little simple to me. I will be reading the series because the concept is interesting. I recommend :). <br /><br /></span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eQVp+E7CNabJOQaM2vGrMXcYf3t1Uo6aTrBCbogL3Ip7VFcv8CSquXZMjQkSSFliS57cencDkY7/Gpmzpe5LeQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qhPbjRZoPc3d6UtJtBTrRtXIquJfJJOlkepbZ1NVZ1GoQuVaqI6i0mKcwMx8rRkV6U4J4111jLEgQIC6frDwog==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16986163731187246200">Yoshihiro Togashi (see also <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6154058._' rel='nofollow noopener'>冨樫 義博</a>) is a manga artist. Credited in Chinese translations as Fu Jian Yi Bo.<br/><br/>He began drawing manga at an early age; while he attended college, the publisher Shueisha recognized his talent. Togashi has authored numerous manga series in different genres during the past three decades. He is perhaps best known for writing and illustrating the YuYu Hakusho and Hunter × Hunte</span>
  <span id="freeText16986163731187246200" style="display:none">Yoshihiro Togashi (see also <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6154058._" rel="nofollow noopener">冨樫 義博</a>) is a manga artist. Credited in Chinese translations as Fu Jian Yi Bo.<br /><br />He began drawing manga at an early age; while he attended college, the publisher Shueisha recognized his talent. Togashi has authored numerous manga series in different genres during the past three decades. He is perhaps best known for writing and illustrating the YuYu Hakusho and Hunter × Hunter series, both of which have been published in the popular Weekly Shōnen Jump magazine. Togashi is married to Naoko Takeuchi, the author of Sailor Moon.</span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
